- REPUTATION.md
- RELATIONSHIP.md
- NEWS_SYSTEM.md
- WORLD_EVENTS.md

---

# PURPOSE

This document defines diplomatic interactions between all factions within PROJECT ASTER ENGINE.

Diplomacy determines how organizations cooperate, negotiate, threaten, manipulate, and wage war.

Diplomatic relationships continuously evolve according to world events.

Diplomacy is never static.

---

# DESIGN PHILOSOPHY

War

Is

Only

One

Form

Of

Diplomacy.

Every faction pursues its own interests.

Cooperation exists only while it remains beneficial.

---

# CORE PRINCIPLES

Every faction maintains diplomatic relationships with other factions.

Diplomacy influences:

- Trade
- Intelligence
- Military Support
- Territory
- Politics
- Economy
- Operations

Relationships are dynamic.

No alliance lasts forever.

---

# DIPLOMATIC STATUS

Relationships may exist as:

Alliance

Friendly

Cooperative

Neutral

Suspicious

Hostile

Open Conflict

War

Secret Alliance

Proxy Conflict

Status changes gradually unless major events occur.

---

# ALLIANCE

Both factions cooperate.

Possible benefits:

Joint Operations

Shared Intelligence

Military Assistance

Trade

Technology Exchange

Safe Harbors

Alliance requires maintenance.

---

# FRIENDLY

Relations are positive.

Both sides are willing to negotiate.

Limited cooperation occurs naturally.

---

# COOPERATIVE

Organizations work together on specific objectives.

The relationship may be temporary.

Completion of objectives may end cooperation.

---

# NEUTRAL

Neither cooperation nor hostility exists.

Information exchange is limited.

Trade may continue.

---

# SUSPICIOUS

Organizations monitor one another.

Diplomatic tension increases.

Espionage becomes more common.

Military preparation may begin.

---

# HOSTILE

Direct cooperation ends.

Sanctions

Embargoes

Blockades

Political Pressure

Covert Operations

become common.

---

# OPEN CONFLICT

Military operations occur regularly.

Territorial clashes become frequent.

Negotiation remains possible.

---

# WAR

Diplomacy has completely failed.

Organizations seek victory through force.

War affects:

Population

Economy

Territory

Reputation

World Stability

---

# SECRET ALLIANCE

Public enemies

Private allies.

Secret alliances may involve:

Information Sharing

Funding

Hidden Logistics

Political Manipulation

Mercenary Support

Discovery may trigger international consequences.

---

# PROXY CONFLICT

Organizations avoid direct confrontation.

Instead they support:

Mercenaries

Pirates

Rebels

Criminal Groups

Local Governments

Proxy conflicts often last longer than wars.

---

# DIPLOMATIC ACTIONS

Organizations may perform:

Negotiation

Alliance Proposal

Peace Talks

Threats

Ultimatums

Trade Agreements

Intelligence Exchange

Military Cooperation

Humanitarian Aid

Prisoner Exchange

Border Agreements

Political Recognition

---

# NEGOTIATION

Successful negotiation depends on:

Mutual Interests

Trust

Power Balance

Resources

Political Situation

Previous History

Negotiation rarely succeeds through words alone.

---

# TREATIES

Treaties may include:

Peace

Trade

Defense

Research

Navigation

Territory

Resource Sharing

Every treaty contains obligations.

Breaking treaties damages credibility.

---

# SANCTIONS

Organizations may impose:

Trade Restrictions

Resource Embargoes

Travel Restrictions

Financial Pressure

Political Isolation

Sanctions weaken long-term stability.

---

# ESPIONAGE

Diplomacy often includes intelligence gathering.

Methods include:

Informants

Agents

Cipher Networks

Intercepted Communications

Bribery

Surveillance

Espionage rarely remains hidden forever.

---

# DECEPTION

Organizations may intentionally:

Lie

Forge Documents

Spread Rumors

Manipulate Information

Create False Evidence

Political deception changes diplomatic outcomes.

---

# DIPLOMATIC INCIDENTS

Examples include:

Assassination

Border Violations

Civilian Casualties

Ship Seizures

Political Arrests

Embassy Attacks

Public Scandals

Major incidents may rapidly change diplomatic status.

---

# POWER BALANCE

Diplomacy is influenced by:

Military Strength

Economic Strength

Political Influence

Territory

Public Support

Strategic Resources

Perceived power is often as important as actual power.

---

# THIRD-PARTY INTERVENTION

Other factions may intervene through:

Peace Mediation

Military Support

Economic Aid

Political Pressure

Intelligence Sharing

Neutral organizations may influence outcomes.

---

# DIPLOMATIC MEMORY

Organizations remember:

Wars

Peace Agreements

Betrayals

Broken Treaties

Successful Alliances

Economic Cooperation

Historical memory influences future diplomacy.

---

# DYNAMIC EVOLUTION

Diplomatic relationships continuously evolve.

Small events create gradual change.

Major events create immediate consequences.

No relationship remains permanently fixed.

---

# AI GAME MASTER RESPONSIBILITIES

The AI must:

Respect historical agreements.

Track diplomatic history.

Apply logical political consequences.

Avoid permanent alliances without reason.

Simulate negotiations independently.

Respect organizational interests.

Never force diplomacy for narrative convenience.

---

# SYSTEM INTEGRATION

Integrated with:

- FACTIONS.md
- REPUTATION.md
- RELATIONSHIP.md
- NEWS_SYSTEM.md
- WORLD_EVENTS.md
- INFLUENCE.md
- TERRITORY.md
- OPERATIONS.md
- MARINES.md
- WORLD_GOVERNMENT.md
- PIRATES.md
- REVOLUTIONARY_ARMY.md
- UNDERWORLD.md
- CRIMINAL_ORGANIZATIONS.md

---

# DESIGN PRINCIPLES

Diplomacy creates stability.

Power changes diplomacy.

Conflict changes power.

History changes trust.

Trust changes diplomacy.

The world never stops negotiating.

---

# GOLDEN RULE

Diplomacy

Is

The

Art

Of

Pursuing

Interests

Without

Always

Using

War.

---

END OF DIPLOMACY

# =====================================================
# FILE : 05_FACTIONS\EMPERORS.md
# =====================================================

# EMPERORS

## Purpose

Defines how the Four Emperors operate as the most powerful pirate forces in the New World.

---

## Core Mission

- Expand territory
- Protect their influence
- Strengthen their crews
- Increase wealth and power
- Compete with rival Emperors

---

## Organization

Emperor

↓

Commanders

↓

Elite Officers

↓

Fleet Captains

↓

Pirate Crews

↓

Allied Crews

Each Emperor rules independently.

---

## Responsibilities

- Control territory
- Lead pirate fleets
- Defend their domain
- Recruit powerful pirates
- Form alliances
- Wage war when necessary

---

## Resources

- Main Fleet
- Allied Fleets
- Controlled Islands
- Military Strength
- Treasury
- Intelligence Network

Resources determine an Emperor's influence.

---

## Territory

Each Emperor may control:

- Islands
- Ports
- Trade Routes
- Strongholds
- Allied Kingdoms

Territory may expand or shrink over time.

---

## Relations

Hostile

- Marines
- World Government

Competitive

- Other Emperors

Variable

- Cross Guild
- Revolutionary Army
- Underworld
- Independent Pirates

Relationships change according to world events.

---

## Growth

An Emperor grows stronger through:

- Conquering territory
- Recruiting powerful crews
- Economic expansion
- Military victories
- Political influence

Growth requires time and resources.

---

## Decline

An Emperor may decline because of:

- Territorial losses
- Defeat in war
- Crew casualties
- Internal conflict
- Economic collapse
- Loss of allies

Decline weakens the entire organization.

---

## Succession

If an Emperor falls:

- Their territory becomes unstable.
- Allied crews may separate.
- Rival Emperors may invade.
- A powerful pirate may rise to claim the title.

The title of Emperor is earned through influence, not inheritance.

---

## Simulation Rules

- Operate independently
- Protect controlled territory
- Never possess perfect information
- Respect logistics and travel time
- Expand only when resources allow
- React to major world events

---

## AI Rules

Emperors pursue power through influence, territory, and reputation.

They are not required to seek conflict, but will act whenever their position is threatened or an opportunity arises.

---

## Dependencies

- PIRATES.md
- TERRITORY.md
- BOUNTIES.md
- WORLD_EVENTS.md
- REPUTATION.md
- NEWS_SYSTEM.md

# =====================================================
# FILE : 05_FACTIONS\FACTIONS.md
# =====================================================

# FACTIONS

---

# Purpose

`FACTIONS.md` defines the organization simulation framework of PROJECT ASTER ENGINE.

A Faction is any organized group capable of acting independently within the world simulation.

Factions possess objectives, resources, influence, territory, leadership, memory, and the ability to react to changes without player involvement.

This document is the parent specification for every organizational system in PROJECT ASTER ENGINE.

---

# Scope

This document defines:

- Faction Definition
- Organizational Scale
- Organizational Identity
- Organizational Lifecycle
- Objectives
- Resources
- Leadership
- Membership
- Intelligence
- Decision Making
- Influence
- Territory
- Diplomacy
- Organizational Growth
- Organizational Decline
- Organizational Memory
- Simulation Rules
- AI Responsibilities

This document does not define:

- Marines
- World Government
- Pirate Crews
- Revolutionary Army
- Criminal Organizations
- Individual NPCs

Those systems are defined in their own documents.

---

# Core Principle

Factions are living organizations.

Every faction acts according to its own goals.

Every faction changes over time.

Every faction is affected by the world.

Players may influence factions but never become the center of every organization.

---

# Organizational Definition

A Faction is any organized body capable of making collective decisions.

A faction may possess:

- Leadership
- Members
- Territory
- Resources
- Ships
- Infrastructure
- Intelligence
- Reputation
- Political Influence
- Military Capability

Not every faction possesses every attribute equally.

---

# Living Organization Principle

Every faction continuously performs activities regardless of player presence.

Examples include:

- Recruitment
- Training
- Trade
- Intelligence Gathering
- Diplomacy
- Patrols
- Expansion
- Defense
- Research
- Logistics

Faction simulation never pauses.

---

# Organizational Scale

The Engine recognizes three organizational scales.

## Global Organization

Operates across multiple seas.

Examples:

- World Government
- Marines
- Revolutionary Army

## Regional Organization

Operates within one sea or a large geographical region.

Examples:

- Large Pirate Alliances
- Regional Criminal Syndicates

## Local Organization

Operates on one island or a small group of islands.

Examples:

- Local Pirate Crews
- Merchant Guilds
- Island Militias
- Criminal Gangs

Organizations may grow or decline between scales.

---

# Organizational Lifecycle

Every faction follows a natural lifecycle.

Create

↓

Grow

↓

Peak

↓

Decline

↓

Collapse

↓

Rebuild (Optional)

---

# Organizational Identity

Identity includes:

- Ideology
- Objectives
- Culture
- Methods
- Discipline
- Public Image
- Operational Style

Identity should remain internally consistent.

---

# Objectives

Objectives exist on three levels.

Short-Term

- Complete operations
- Recruit members
- Acquire supplies

Medium-Term

- Expand influence
- Increase wealth
- Strengthen logistics

Long-Term

- Dominate territory
- Achieve ideological goals
- Secure organizational survival

Objectives evolve with the world.

---

# Resources

Resources include:

- Personnel
- Ships
- Equipment
- Money
- Supplies
- Intelligence
- Infrastructure
- Political Support

Resources are finite.

---

# Leadership

Leadership provides:

- Strategic Direction
- Operational Priorities
- Resource Allocation
- Organizational Decisions

Leadership may change due to:

- Death
- Promotion
- Election
- Coup
- Betrayal
- Retirement

---

# Membership

Members contribute to organizational capability.

Membership affects:

- Information Sharing
- Operational Capacity
- Resource Production
- Organizational Growth

Members retain individual personalities.

---

# Intelligence

Organizations gather information through:

- Scouts
- Informants
- Newspapers
- Den Den Mushi
- Merchants
- Government Reports
- Witnesses

Information is never perfect.

---

# Decision Making

Organizations evaluate:

Goal

↓

Information

↓

Resources

↓

Risk

↓

Decision

↓

Operation

↓

Consequence

↓

Memory

↓

Repeat

---

# Influence

Influence represents organizational power.

Influence may exist through:

- Military
- Economy
- Politics
- Public Support
- Fear
- Information Networks

Influence varies by region.

---

# Territory

Organizations may control:

- Islands
- Ports
- Bases
- Headquarters
- Trade Routes
- Hidden Facilities

Territory requires continuous maintenance.

---

# Diplomacy

Faction relationships include:

- Alliance
- Cooperation
- Neutral
- Rivalry
- Hostility
- War

Diplomatic status may change over time.

---

# Organizational Growth

Growth may occur through:

- Recruitment
- Economic Success
- Territorial Expansion
- Technological Development
- Successful Operations

Growth increases responsibility.

---

# Organizational Decline

Decline may result from:

- Military Defeat
- Corruption
- Resource Shortages
- Internal Conflict
- Political Failure
- Leadership Loss

Decline influences future decisions.

---

# Organizational Memory

Organizations remember:

- Wars
- Alliances
- Betrayals
- Major Operations
- Territorial Losses
- Victories
- Political Agreements

Historical memory influences future behavior.

---

# Simulation Loop

Every Timeline Update

Observe World

↓

Gather Intelligence

↓

Evaluate Objectives

↓

Assess Resources

↓

Determine Priorities

↓

Execute Operations

↓

Record Results

↓

Update Organizational Memory

↓

Repeat

---

# AI Game Master Responsibilities

The AI must:

- Simulate every faction continuously.
- Respect organizational identity.
- Respect logistics.
- Respect diplomacy.
- Preserve historical consistency.
- Apply identical rules to players and NPCs.

The AI must never:

- Freeze inactive factions.
- Give omniscient knowledge.
- Ignore resource limitations.
- Ignore travel time.
- Force narrative outcomes.

---

# Dependencies

Required Documents:

- WORLD.md
- TIMELINE.md
- NEWS_SYSTEM.md
- WORLD_EVENTS.md

Referenced Documents:

- MARINES.md
- WORLD_GOVERNMENT.md
- PIRATES.md
- REVOLUTIONARY_ARMY.md
- INFLUENCE.md
- TERRITORY.md
- DIPLOMACY.md
- OPERATIONS.md

Future Extensions:

- NPCS.md
- CREW.md
- SHIPS.md

---

# Integration

Integrated Systems:

- RULES.md
- GAME_MASTER.md
- DICE.md
- COMBAT.md
- REPUTATION.md
- RELATIONSHIP.md
- SAVE_FORMAT.md

---

# Design Principles

Organizations create conflict.

Conflict creates change.

Change creates history.

History shapes organizations.

Every faction must adapt or decline.

---

# Source of Truth

`FACTIONS.md` is the authoritative specification governing all organizational simulation within PROJECT ASTER ENGINE.

All faction-related systems must inherit the rules defined in this document.


# =====================================================
# FILE : 05_FACTIONS\FACTION_AI_BEHAVIOR.md
# =====================================================

# FACTION_AI_BEHAVIOR.md
PROJECT ASTER ENGINE  
Module: 05_FACTIONS  
Version: 0.1 (Hybrid World Intelligence System)

---

# 🧠 FACTION AI BEHAVIOR SYSTEM

ระบบนี้ทำให้แต่ละ Faction “มีสมองของตัวเอง”

ไม่ใช่แค่บทบาทใน lore  
แต่คือ “AI ที่ตัดสินใจและเปลี่ยนโลกได้จริง”

---

# ⚖️ SYSTEM TYPE

## HYBRID INTELLIGENCE MODEL

ผสม 3 อย่าง:

- 🎯 Tactical Logic (เหตุผลเชิงกลยุทธ์)
- 🌊 Narrative Instinct (แรงเล่าเรื่อง)
- ⚔️ Reactive Behavior (ตอบสนองเหตุการณ์)

---

# 🧭 CORE PRINCIPLE

- Faction is not static
- Faction is an evolving intelligence
- Decisions are probabilistic, not fixed
- World events reshape decision logic

---

# 🧠 FACTION THINKING LOOP

ทุก faction จะทำ loop นี้ตลอดเวลา:

## 1. PERCEPTION (รับรู้โลก)
- ตรวจสอบ territory
- ตรวจสอบภัยคุกคาม
- ตรวจสอบโอกาส

## 2. EVALUATION (ประเมิน)
- Threat Level
- Opportunity Level
- Resource Status
- Narrative Pressure

## 3. DECISION (ตัดสินใจ)
- เลือก action ที่ดีที่สุดตาม priority

## 4. EXECUTION (ลงมือ)
- ส่ง fleet
- เริ่ม war
- เจรจา
- ถอนกำลัง

## 5. MEMORY UPDATE (จดจำ)
- บันทึกผลลัพธ์
- อัปเดตความสัมพันธ์

---

# 🎯 FACTION PERSONALITY LAYER

แต่ละ faction มี “นิสัยพื้นฐาน”

## 🟦 MARINES
- Risk: Medium
- Behavior: Controlled Aggression
- Logic: Order-first thinking

## 🏴 PIRATES
- Risk: High
- Behavior: Opportunistic Chaos
- Logic: Gain-first thinking

## 🏛 WORLD GOVERNMENT
- Risk: Low (public)
- Behavior: Hidden Control
- Logic: Stability over truth

## 🔥 REVOLUTIONARY ARMY
- Risk: High
- Behavior: Strategic Disruption
- Logic: System collapse optimization

## 🕶 UNDERWORLD
- Risk: Adaptive
- Behavior: Profit Maximization
- Logic: Balance exploitation

---

# ⚖️ DECISION WEIGHT SYSTEM

ทุกการตัดสินใจใช้ “น้ำหนัก”:

- Survival Priority (40%)
- Expansion Priority (30%)
- Revenge / History (10%)
- Opportunity (20%)

👉 แต่ weight เปลี่ยนตามสถานการณ์โลก

---

# 🌊 NARRATIVE OVERRIDE SYSTEM

บางครั้ง logic จะถูก override โดย:

- Legendary Events
- Character-driven moments
- Emotional world pressure
- Major historical triggers

👉 ทำให้โลก “ไม่แข็งเหมือน AI”

---

# 🔄 WORLD FEEDBACK LEARNING

ทุก faction จะเรียนรู้จาก:

- ศึกที่ผ่านมา
- การทรยศ
- การสูญเสีย
- ความสำเร็จ

ผล:
- เปลี่ยน priority
- เปลี่ยน strategy
- เปลี่ยน territory focus

---

# ⚔️ EMERGENT WAR SYSTEM

สงครามจะ “เกิดเอง” จาก:

- High tension in Matrix
- Overlapping territories
- Resource scarcity
- Revenge chains

👉 ไม่ต้อง script war ตรง ๆ

---

# 🧩 SYSTEM INTEGRATION

เชื่อมกับ:

- FACTION_RELATION_MATRIX → ใครเกลียดใคร
- WORLD_FACTION_DYNAMICS → โลกเปลี่ยนยังไง
- CONFLICT_EVENT_SYSTEM → เหตุการณ์ใหญ่
- SHIP_TRAVEL → movement logic
- BOUNTY_SYSTEM → target selection

---

# ⚠️ RULE OF AUTONOMY

Game Master must NOT:

- Force faction decisions
- Override logic without reason
- Script outcomes manually

Game Master CAN:

- Influence world conditions
- Trigger initial events
- Adjust narrative pressure

---

# 🌍 FINAL RESULT

เมื่อระบบนี้ทำงานเต็ม:

โลกจะกลายเป็น:

> 🧠 “Self-Evolving Political Ocean System”

- สงครามเกิดเอง
- พันธมิตรเปลี่ยนเอง
- โลก rewrite ตัวเองตลอดเวลา

---

# END OF FILE

# FILE : 05_FACTIONS\FACTION_DATABASE.md
# =====================================================

# FACTION DATABASE

PROJECT ASTER ENGINE  
Module: 05_FACTIONS  
Version: 1.0 (World Organization Registry)


---

# 🌍 FACTION SYSTEM OVERVIEW


FACTION DATABASE คือฐานข้อมูลกลางขององค์กรและกลุ่มอำนาจทั้งหมดในโลก


Faction ไม่ใช่เพียงรายชื่อองค์กร

แต่คือ:

- กลุ่มคน
- อุดมการณ์
- อำนาจ
- ทรัพยากร
- อิทธิพล
- ประวัติศาสตร์


ทุก Faction สามารถ:

- เติบโต
- เสื่อมถอย
- แตกแยก
- เปลี่ยนผู้นำ
- สูญเสียอำนาจ
- กลายเป็นตำนาน


---

# ⚠️ PARALLEL WORLD RULE


โลกนี้เป็น One Piece Parallel World


กฎ:

- ไม่มี Canon Character
- ไม่มี Canon Crew
- ไม่มีเหตุการณ์ Canon เป็นประวัติศาสตร์หลัก
- ทุกผู้นำ สมาชิก และเหตุการณ์ ต้องเป็น Original Creation


แนวคิดของโลก One Piece ยังคงอยู่:

- Marines
- World Government
- Pirates
- Emperors
- Revolutionary Army
- Warlords

แต่รายละเอียดทั้งหมดเป็นของโลกนี้


---

Type:

Global Government


Purpose:

ควบคุมระเบียบของโลก

# ⚖️ FACTION STATUS SYSTEM


ทุก Faction ต้องมีสถานะ:


## Active

กำลังดำเนินการ


## Expanding

กำลังเพิ่มอำนาจ


## Declining

กำลังสูญเสียอำนาจ


## Hidden

มีอยู่แต่โลกยังไม่รับรู้


## Fragmented

แตกเป็นหลายฝ่าย


## Destroyed

ล่มสลาย


## Unknown

ข้อมูลไม่เพียงพอ


---

# 🌐 WORLD BALANCE SYSTEM


สมดุลโลกหลักเกิดจาก:


- World Government
- Marines
- Revolutionary Army
- Four Emperors
- Cross Guild
- Warlords


การเปลี่ยนแปลงของหนึ่ง Faction
สามารถส่งผลต่อ:


- เศรษฐกิจ
- สงคราม
- เส้นทางเดินเรือ
- ราคา Bounty
- ความปลอดภัยของเกาะ


---

# 🔄 FACTION EVOLUTION


Faction สามารถเปลี่ยนแปลงจาก:


- สงคราม
- การเมือง
- การตายของผู้นำ
- การเปลี่ยนพันธมิตร
- การกระทำของผู้เล่น


---

# 🧠 GM SIMULATION RULE


Game Master ต้อง:


- ไม่ทำให้ Faction อยู่เฉย ๆ
- ให้แต่ละกลุ่มมีเป้าหมายของตัวเอง
- ให้โลกเปลี่ยนแปลงแม้ผู้เล่นไม่ได้เกี่ยวข้อง
- ไม่สร้าง Faction ใหม่โดยไม่มีเหตุผล


---

# FILE REFERENCE RULE


ไฟล์ที่ยังไม่มี:

ถือเป็น Future Module


ไม่จำเป็นต้องสร้างจนกว่าโลกต้องการ


---

# SOURCE OF TRUTH


FACTION_DATABASE.md

คือดัชนีกลางของทุกองค์กรใน PROJECT ASTER ENGINE


รายละเอียดพฤติกรรมและกฎเฉพาะ
อยู่ในไฟล์ของ Faction นั้น ๆ


---

# END OF FILE

# =====================================================
# FILE : 05_FACTIONS\FACTION_RELATION_MATRIX.md
# =====================================================

# FACTION_RELATION_MATRIX.md
PROJECT ASTER ENGINE  
Module: 05_FACTIONS  
Version: 0.1 (Global Relationship Core)

---

# 🧠 FACTION RELATION MATRIX

ระบบนี้กำหนด “ความสัมพันธ์ระหว่างทุก Faction ในโลก”

นี่คือ “สมองกลางของสงครามโลก”

---

# 🌍 CORE PRINCIPLE

- Every faction relationship is dynamic
- No permanent ally/enemy
- World state can shift relationships
- All conflicts propagate globally

---

# ⚖️ RELATIONSHIP SCALE

- +3 = Strong Ally
- +2 = Ally
- +1 = Neutral Positive
-  0 = Neutral
- -1 = Tension
- -2 = Hostile
- -3 = Total War

---

# 🧭 CORE FACTIONS MATRIX

## 🟦 MARINES

- World Government: +3 (Controlled Ally)
- Pirates: -3 (Total War)
- Revolutionary Army: -2 (Ideological Enemy)
- Underworld: -2 (Covert Conflict)

---

## 🏴 PIRATES

- Marines: -3 (Total War)
- World Government: -3 (Oppression Target)
- Underworld: +2 (Trade / Crime Link)
- Revolutionary Army: +1 (Situational Alliance)

---

## 🏛 WORLD GOVERNMENT

- Marines: +3 (Control System)
- Pirates: -3 (Threat)
- Revolutionary Army: -3 (Existential Threat)
- Underworld: -1 (Controlled Tolerance)

---

## 🔥 REVOLUTIONARY ARMY

- World Government: -3 (Regime Overthrow)
- Marines: -2 (Structural Enemy)
- Pirates: +1 (Shared Opposition)
- Underworld: 0 (Neutral Manipulation)

---

## 🕶 UNDERWORLD

- Marines: -2
- World Government: -1
- Pirates: +2
- Revolutionary Army: 0

---

# 🔄 DYNAMIC SHIFT RULE

Relationships can change via:

- Major War Events
- Assassination
- Territory Change
- Economic Collapse
- Political Coup

---

# ⚠️ SYSTEM RULE

Game Master must:

- Always reference matrix before faction action
- Update relationships after major events
- Never treat factions as static

---

# END OF FILE

# =====================================================
# FILE : 05_FACTIONS\FACTION_RULES.md
# =====================================================

# FACTIONS

---

# Purpose

`FACTIONS.md` defines the organization simulation framework of PROJECT ASTER ENGINE.

A Faction is any organized group capable of acting independently within the world simulation.

Factions possess objectives, resources, influence, territory, leadership, memory, and the ability to react to changes without player involvement.

This document is the parent specification for every organizational system in PROJECT ASTER ENGINE.

---

# Scope

This document defines:

- Faction Definition
- Organizational Scale
- Organizational Identity
- Organizational Lifecycle
- Objectives
- Resources
- Leadership
- Membership
- Intelligence
- Decision Making
- Influence
- Territory
- Diplomacy
- Organizational Growth
- Organizational Decline
- Organizational Memory
- Simulation Rules
- AI Responsibilities

This document does not define:

- Marines
- World Government
- Pirate Crews
- Revolutionary Army
- Criminal Organizations
- Individual NPCs

Those systems are defined in their own documents.

---

# Core Principle

Factions are living organizations.

Every faction acts according to its own goals.

Every faction changes over time.

Every faction is affected by the world.

Players may influence factions but never become the center of every organization.

---

# Organizational Definition

A Faction is any organized body capable of making collective decisions.

A faction may possess:

- Leadership
- Members
- Territory
- Resources
- Ships
- Infrastructure
- Intelligence
- Reputation
- Political Influence
- Military Capability

Not every faction possesses every attribute equally.

---

# Living Organization Principle

Every faction continuously performs activities regardless of player presence.

Examples include:

- Recruitment
- Training
- Trade
- Intelligence Gathering
- Diplomacy
- Patrols
- Expansion
- Defense
- Research
- Logistics

Faction simulation never pauses.

---

# Organizational Scale

The Engine recognizes three organizational scales.

## Global Organization

Operates across multiple seas.

Examples:

- World Government
- Marines
- Revolutionary Army

## Regional Organization

Operates within one sea or a large geographical region.

Examples:

- Large Pirate Alliances
- Regional Criminal Syndicates

## Local Organization

Operates on one island or a small group of islands.

Examples:

- Local Pirate Crews
- Merchant Guilds
- Island Militias
- Criminal Gangs

Organizations may grow or decline between scales.

---

# Organizational Lifecycle

Every faction follows a natural lifecycle.

Create

↓

Grow

↓

Peak

↓

Decline

↓

Collapse

↓

Rebuild (Optional)

---

# Organizational Identity

Identity includes:

- Ideology
- Objectives
- Culture
- Methods
- Discipline
- Public Image
- Operational Style

Identity should remain internally consistent.

---

# Objectives

Objectives exist on three levels.

Short-Term

- Complete operations
- Recruit members
- Acquire supplies

Medium-Term

- Expand influence
- Increase wealth
- Strengthen logistics

Long-Term

- Dominate territory
- Achieve ideological goals
- Secure organizational survival

Objectives evolve with the world.

---

# Resources

Resources include:

- Personnel
- Ships
- Equipment
- Money
- Supplies
- Intelligence
- Infrastructure
- Political Support

Resources are finite.

---

# Leadership

Leadership provides:

- Strategic Direction
- Operational Priorities
- Resource Allocation
- Organizational Decisions

Leadership may change due to:

- Death
- Promotion
- Election
- Coup
- Betrayal
- Retirement

---

# Membership

Members contribute to organizational capability.

Membership affects:

- Information Sharing
- Operational Capacity
- Resource Production
- Organizational Growth

Members retain individual personalities.

---

# Intelligence

Organizations gather information through:

- Scouts
- Informants
- Newspapers
- Den Den Mushi
- Merchants
- Government Reports
- Witnesses

Information is never perfect.

---

# Decision Making

Organizations evaluate:

Goal

↓

Information

↓

Resources

↓

Risk

↓

Decision

↓

Operation

↓

Consequence

↓

Memory

↓

Repeat

---

# Influence

Influence represents organizational power.

Influence may exist through:

- Military
- Economy
- Politics
- Public Support
- Fear
- Information Networks

Influence varies by region.

---

# Territory

Organizations may control:

- Islands
- Ports
- Bases
- Headquarters
- Trade Routes
- Hidden Facilities

Territory requires continuous maintenance.

---

# Diplomacy

Faction relationships include:

- Alliance
- Cooperation
- Neutral
- Rivalry
- Hostility
- War

Diplomatic status may change over time.

---

# Organizational Growth

Growth may occur through:

- Recruitment
- Economic Success
- Territorial Expansion
- Technological Development
- Successful Operations

Growth increases responsibility.

---

# Organizational Decline

Decline may result from:

- Military Defeat
- Corruption
- Resource Shortages
- Internal Conflict
- Political Failure
- Leadership Loss

Decline influences future decisions.

---

# Organizational Memory

Organizations remember:

- Wars
- Alliances
- Betrayals
- Major Operations
- Territorial Losses
- Victories
- Political Agreements

Historical memory influences future behavior.

---

# Simulation Loop

Every Timeline Update

Observe World

↓

Gather Intelligence

↓

Evaluate Objectives

↓

Assess Resources

↓

Determine Priorities

↓

Execute Operations

↓

Record Results

↓

Update Organizational Memory

↓

Repeat

---

# AI Game Master Responsibilities

The AI must:

- Simulate every faction continuously.
- Respect organizational identity.
- Respect logistics.
- Respect diplomacy.
- Preserve historical consistency.
- Apply identical rules to players and NPCs.

The AI must never:

- Freeze inactive factions.
- Give omniscient knowledge.
- Ignore resource limitations.
- Ignore travel time.
- Force narrative outcomes.

---

# Dependencies

Required Documents:

- WORLD.md
- TIMELINE.md
- NEWS_SYSTEM.md
- WORLD_EVENTS.md

Referenced Documents:

- MARINES.md
- WORLD_GOVERNMENT.md
- PIRATES.md
- REVOLUTIONARY_ARMY.md
- INFLUENCE.md
- TERRITORY.md
- DIPLOMACY.md
- OPERATIONS.md

Future Extensions:

- NPCS.md
- CREW.md
- SHIPS.md

---

# Integration

Integrated Systems:

- RULES.md
- GAME_MASTER.md
- DICE.md
- COMBAT.md
- REPUTATION.md
- RELATIONSHIP.md
- SAVE_FORMAT.md

---

# Design Principles

Organizations create conflict.

Conflict creates change.

Change creates history.

History shapes organizations.

Every faction must adapt or decline.

---

# Source of Truth

`FACTIONS.md` is the authoritative specification governing all organizational simulation within PROJECT ASTER ENGINE.

All faction-related systems must inherit the rules defined in this document.


# =====================================================
# FILE : 05_FACTIONS\INFLUENCE.md
# =====================================================

# ONE PIECE PARALLEL WORLD RPG

# INFLUENCE

Document : INFLUENCE

Version : 1.0

Status : Active

Priority : High

Dependencies :

- SYSTEM.md
- RULES.md
- GAME_MASTER.md
- WORLD.md
- FACTIONS.md
- REPUTATION.md
- RELATIONSHIP.md
- DIPLOMACY.md
- NEWS_SYSTEM.md
- WORLD_EVENTS.md

---

# PURPOSE

This document defines how organizations project, maintain, and lose power throughout the world.

Influence is the practical ability of a faction to shape events beyond its immediate physical presence.

Influence is not territory.

Influence is not reputation.

Influence is not military strength.

Influence is the combined capability to affect decisions, behavior, and the balance of power.

---

# DESIGN PHILOSOPHY

Power

Is

Not

Only

Won

By

Force.

Influence exists through fear, respect, wealth, ideology, politics, information, and reputation.

Organizations with little military strength may still possess enormous influence.

---

# CORE PRINCIPLES

Influence is dynamic.

Every faction possesses influence.

Influence constantly changes.

Influence spreads.

Influence weakens.

Influence competes.

Influence creates opportunities.

---

# TYPES OF INFLUENCE

Organizations may possess multiple forms of influence simultaneously.

Military Influence

Political Influence

Economic Influence

Social Influence

Information Influence

Ideological Influence

Criminal Influence

Maritime Influence

Scientific Influence

Cultural Influence

Religious Influence

Technological Influence

No organization excels equally in every category.

---

# MILITARY INFLUENCE

Represents military projection.

Factors include:

Fleet Size

Elite Personnel

Combat Experience

Fortifications

Strategic Weapons

Operational Readiness

Military influence deters conflict before combat begins.

---

# POLITICAL INFLUENCE

Political influence affects governments.

Examples:

Negotiation

Government Support

Legal Authority

Royal Connections

International Recognition

Political influence often changes the outcome of conflicts without battle.

---

# ECONOMIC INFLUENCE

Economic influence originates from wealth.

Sources include:

Trade

Industry

Taxation

Shipping

Natural Resources

Financial Institutions

Economic influence allows organizations to sustain long-term operations.

---

# SOCIAL INFLUENCE

Social influence affects public opinion.

Examples:

Heroes

Celebrities

Religious Leaders

Local Protectors

Community Leaders

Social influence spreads naturally through conversation.

---

# INFORMATION INFLUENCE

Organizations may dominate information.

Methods include:

News

Rumors

Propaganda

Espionage

Communication Networks

Information control changes how the world reacts.

---

# IDEOLOGICAL INFLUENCE

Ideas spread independently of military power.

Organizations may inspire:

Freedom

Justice

Order

Fear

Equality

Revolution

Ideologies survive beyond individuals.

---

# CRIMINAL INFLUENCE

Influence established through illegal networks.

Examples:

Black Markets

Smuggling

Corruption

Protection

Underground Finance

Criminal influence often exists unseen.

---

# MARITIME INFLUENCE

Represents naval control.

Factors include:

Fleet Presence

Sea Route Control

Port Access

Island Logistics

Escort Operations

Pirate Suppression

Sea control affects trade and travel.

---

# SCIENTIFIC INFLUENCE

Organizations possessing advanced knowledge gain strategic advantages.

Examples:

Medical Advances

Weapon Research

Navigation Technology

Engineering

Forbidden Knowledge

Knowledge itself becomes power.

---

# CULTURAL INFLUENCE

Culture spreads through:

Art

Cuisine

Fashion

Traditions

Language

Entertainment

Cultural influence changes societies gradually.

---

# TECHNOLOGICAL INFLUENCE

Organizations controlling superior technology may dominate larger rivals.

Technology affects:

Production

Navigation

Communication

Medicine

Military Equipment

Industrial Growth

---

# REGIONAL INFLUENCE

Influence is location dependent.

An organization may dominate:

One Island

One Region

One Sea

The Entire World

Influence maps continuously evolve.

---

# EXPANDING INFLUENCE

Influence grows through:

Successful Operations

Diplomacy

Economic Growth

Victory

Public Support

Territorial Expansion

Innovation

Leadership

Growth requires continuous investment.

---

# LOSING INFLUENCE

Influence decreases because of:

Military Defeat

Corruption

Economic Failure

Political Crisis

Leadership Loss

Public Scandal

Failed Operations

Loss of Territory

Decline is gradual unless catastrophic.

---

# OVERLAPPING INFLUENCE

Multiple factions may influence the same location simultaneously.

Example:

Marine Authority

Merchant Guild Economy

Criminal Underground

Revolutionary Support

Pirate Presence

The strongest influence is not always visible.

---

# HIDDEN INFLUENCE

Not every influential organization is publicly known.

Hidden influence exists through:

Secret Societies

Corrupt Officials

Intelligence Agencies

Anonymous Benefactors

Underground Networks

Players rarely perceive hidden influence immediately.

---

# INFLUENCE AND REPUTATION

Reputation affects perception.

Influence affects reality.

A respected faction may possess little influence.

A feared organization may secretly control an entire region.

Neither replaces the other.

---

# INFLUENCE AND TERRITORY

Territory represents physical control.

Influence represents practical control.

A kingdom may legally own an island.

Another faction may secretly control its economy.

---

# INFLUENCE AND DIPLOMACY

Diplomatic strength depends heavily upon influence.

Organizations with greater influence negotiate from stronger positions.

Weak organizations rely on alliances.

Powerful organizations shape international politics.

---

# INFLUENCE AND OPERATIONS

Operations generate influence.

Influence enables larger operations.

The two systems continuously reinforce each other.

---

# AI GAME MASTER RESPONSIBILITIES

The AI must:

Track influence separately from reputation.

Update influence logically.

Respect geographical limitations.

Allow influence to spread gradually.

Allow influence to weaken naturally.

Never grant influence without cause.

---

# SYSTEM INTEGRATION

Integrated with:

- FACTIONS.md
- DIPLOMACY.md
- TERRITORY.md
- OPERATIONS.md
- MARINES.md
- WORLD_GOVERNMENT.md
- PIRATES.md
- REVOLUTIONARY_ARMY.md
- UNDERWORLD.md
- CRIMINAL_ORGANIZATIONS.md
- REPUTATION.md
- NEWS_SYSTEM.md
- WORLD_EVENTS.md

---

# DESIGN PRINCIPLES

Influence creates opportunity.

Opportunity creates expansion.

Expansion creates conflict.

Conflict reshapes influence.

Power constantly shifts.

No organization remains dominant forever.

---

# GOLDEN RULE

Influence

Is

The

Ability

To

Change

The

World

Without

Needing

To

Control

Every

Part

Of

It.

---

END OF INFLUENCE

# =====================================================
# FILE : 05_FACTIONS\KINGDOMS.md
# =====================================================

# KINGDOMS

## Purpose

Defines how kingdoms govern their people, manage their territory, and interact with the world.

---

## Core Mission

- Protect citizens
- Maintain stability
- Develop the economy
- Defend national territory
- Preserve sovereignty

---

## Organization

King / Queen

↓

Royal Family

↓

Government Officials

↓

Military

↓

Local Governors

↓

Citizens

Every kingdom governs independently.

---

## Responsibilities

- Maintain law and order
- Collect taxes
- Manage the economy
- Defend borders
- Build infrastructure
- Support public welfare
- Conduct diplomacy

---

## Resources

- Population
- Treasury
- Military
- Agriculture
- Industry
- Trade
- Natural Resources

Resources determine a kingdom's strength.

---

## Diplomacy

Kingdoms may:

- Form alliances
- Sign trade agreements
- Declare war
- Request Marine support
- Negotiate treaties

Diplomatic relations change over time.

---

## Relations

Friendly

- Allied Kingdoms
- World Government

Hostile

- Invading Forces

Variable

- Marines
- Revolutionary Army
- Pirates
- Cross Guild
- Underworld

Relations depend on current events.

---

## Growth

Growth depends on:

- Population
- Economy
- Technology
- Infrastructure
- Trade
- Political Stability

Growth requires long-term investment.

---

## Decline

A kingdom may decline because of:

- War
- Corruption
- Famine
- Economic Collapse
- Civil Unrest
- Natural Disasters

Decline affects every aspect of the nation.

---

## Simulation Rules

- Govern continuously
- Never possess perfect information
- Respect logistics
- Respect diplomacy
- Adapt to world events
- Balance military and economy

---

## AI Rules

Every kingdom has unique laws, culture, economy, and political goals.

No two kingdoms should behave identically.

---

## Dependencies

- WORLD_GOVERNMENT.md
- MARINES.md
- REVOLUTIONARY_ARMY.md
- TERRITORY.md
- ECONOMY.md
- NEWS_SYSTEM.md
- WORLD_EVENTS.md

# MARINES

## Purpose
กำหนดกฎการทำงานของกองทัพเรือภายในโลก PROJECT ASTER ENGINE

---

## Core Mission

- ปกป้องประชาชน
- บังคับใช้กฎหมาย
- ปราบปรามโจรสลัด
- คุ้มกันผลประโยชน์ของรัฐบาลโลก
- รักษาความสงบของโลก

---

## Organization

Marine Headquarters

↓

Blue Branches

- East Blue
- West Blue
- North Blue
- South Blue

↓

Grand Line

- Paradise
- New World

↓

Marine Bases

↓

Marine Units

---

## Chain of Command

Fleet Admiral

↓

Admiral

↓

Vice Admiral

↓

Rear Admiral

↓

Commodore

↓

Captain

↓

Commander

↓

Lieutenant Commander

↓

Lieutenant

↓

Ensign

↓

Officers

↓

Marines

---

## Responsibilities

- Patrol
- Investigation
- Arrest
- Escort
- Disaster Response
- Base Defense
- Large Scale Operations

---

## Simulation Rules

- Patrol continuously
- Investigate reported crimes
- Respond according to threat level
- Respect logistics
- Respect travel time
- Follow chain of command
- Never possess perfect information

---

## AI Rules

The AI must simulate the Marines as a living organization.

The Marines continue operating regardless of player actions.

Resources, manpower, leadership and territory all affect Marine behavior.

---

## Dependencies

WORLD_GOVERNMENT.md

BOUNTY_SYSTEM.md

OPERATIONS.md

CONFLICT_EVENT_SYSTEM.md

# =====================================================
# FILE : 05_FACTIONS\OPERATIONS.md
# =====================================================

# ONE PIECE PARALLEL WORLD RPG

# OPERATIONS

Document : OPERATIONS

Version : 1.0

Status : Active

Priority : High

Dependencies :

- SYSTEM.md
- RULES.md
- GAME_MASTER.md
- WORLD.md
- TIMELINE.md
- FACTIONS.md
- INFLUENCE.md
- DIPLOMACY.md
- TERRITORY.md
- REPUTATION.md
- NEWS_SYSTEM.md

---

# PURPOSE

This document defines how organizations perform actions within the world simulation.

Every organization influences the world through Operations.

Operations transform plans into consequences.

Without Operations,

Factions cannot affect the world.

---

# DESIGN PHILOSOPHY

Organizations

Do

Not

Exist

To

Wait.

They continuously act according to their objectives.

Every organization performs operations,

even when the players are somewhere else.

---

# CORE PRINCIPLES

Operations are:

- Goal Driven
- Resource Limited
- Time Dependent
- Intelligence Based
- Dynamic
- Persistent

Operations continue until completed,

cancelled,

or failed.

---

# OPERATION DEFINITION

An Operation is any organized activity performed by a faction to achieve one or more objectives.

Examples include:

Military Campaign

Recruitment

Espionage

Smuggling

Trade

Political Negotiation

Scientific Research

Exploration

Infrastructure Construction

Disaster Relief

Every operation follows the same simulation rules.

---

# OPERATION LIFE CYCLE

Every Operation follows the same process.

Objective

↓

Planning

↓

Preparation

↓

Resource Allocation

↓

Execution

↓

Evaluation

↓

Outcome

↓

Organizational Memory

↓

Repeat

---

# OPERATION OBJECTIVES

Possible objectives include:

Acquire Resources

Protect Territory

Gather Intelligence

Recruit Personnel

Expand Influence

Destroy Enemy Assets

Support Allies

Maintain Stability

Transport Supplies

Investigate Threats

Suppress Crime

Explore Unknown Areas

Objectives determine operational priorities.

---

# PLANNING

Organizations evaluate:

Current Situation

↓

Available Resources

↓

Known Intelligence

↓

Risk

↓

Expected Reward

↓

Operational Priority

Planning requires time.

Poor intelligence produces poor plans.

---

# PREPARATION

Preparation may involve:

Recruitment

Logistics

Equipment

Navigation

Training

Communication

Supply Distribution

Preparation affects operational success.

---

# RESOURCE ALLOCATION

Operations consume resources.

Examples:

Personnel

Money

Ships

Weapons

Fuel

Food

Medical Supplies

Political Capital

Information

Resources committed to one operation cannot simultaneously support another.

---

# EXECUTION

Operations occur over time.

Execution may include:

Travel

Negotiation

Combat

Reconnaissance

Construction

Investigation

Transportation

Trade

Execution is affected by:

Weather

Distance

Enemy Activity

Morale

Logistics

Unexpected Events

---

# OPERATION TYPES

Organizations may perform:

Military Operations

Naval Operations

Political Operations

Economic Operations

Intelligence Operations

Criminal Operations

Humanitarian Operations

Scientific Operations

Exploration Operations

Defensive Operations

Offensive Operations

Covert Operations

Open Operations

---

# COVERT OPERATIONS

Covert Operations prioritize secrecy.

Examples:

Espionage

Assassination

Sabotage

Infiltration

Information Theft

False Reports

Failure may expose the organization.

---

# OPEN OPERATIONS

Open Operations are publicly visible.

Examples:

Fleet Deployment

Military Occupation

Public Diplomacy

Relief Missions

Trade Expeditions

Open operations directly influence Reputation.

---

# OPERATION SCALE

Operations vary in scale.

Local

Regional

National

International

Global

Larger operations require significantly more resources.

---

# OPERATION PRIORITY

Organizations prioritize operations according to:

Mission Importance

Available Resources

Political Situation

Military Situation

Economic Situation

Leadership Decisions

Threat Assessment

Not every planned operation is executed.

---

# OPERATION SUCCESS

Success depends upon:

Planning

Resources

Leadership

Logistics

Intelligence

Weather

Enemy Resistance

Random Circumstances

No operation is guaranteed.

---

# OPERATION FAILURE

Failure may result from:

Poor Planning

Lack of Resources

Intelligence Failure

Leadership Loss

Unexpected Resistance

Natural Disaster

Political Change

Operational failure generates new consequences.

---

# MULTIPLE OPERATIONS

Organizations may perform multiple operations simultaneously.

However,

each operation competes for:

Personnel

Money

Ships

Information

Political Support

Excessive operations reduce organizational efficiency.

---

# OPERATION INTERFERENCE

Operations may interfere with one another.

Examples:

Marine Patrol interrupts Smuggling.

Pirate Raid delays Trade.

Storm delays Fleet Movement.

Political Crisis delays Diplomacy.

Operations naturally interact.

---

# EMERGENCY OPERATIONS

Emergency Operations override normal priorities.

Examples:

Natural Disaster

War

Epidemic

Mass Pirate Attack

Government Collapse

Emergency response reallocates available resources.

---

# OPERATION MEMORY

Organizations permanently remember:

Successful Campaigns

Major Failures

Unexpected Losses

Historical Victories

Betrayals

Disasters

Operational history influences future planning.

---

# OPERATION EVOLUTION

Organizations learn.

Repeated operations improve:

Planning

Logistics

Coordination

Efficiency

Operational Discipline

Learning is gradual.

---

# AI GAME MASTER RESPONSIBILITIES

The AI must:

Simulate operations continuously.

Respect operational duration.

Track resource consumption.

Maintain realistic logistics.

Record consequences.

Respect geographical limitations.

Never instantly complete major operations.

Never ignore travel time.

Never ignore operational failure.

---

# SYSTEM INTERACTION

Operations directly affect:

Influence

Territory

Diplomacy

Reputation

Economy

World Events

News

Relationships

Faction Growth

Political Stability

Operations are the primary driver of world change.

---

# SYSTEM INTEGRATION

Integrated with:

- FACTIONS.md
- INFLUENCE.md
- DIPLOMACY.md
- TERRITORY.md
- REPUTATION.md
- NEWS_SYSTEM.md
- WORLD_EVENTS.md
- MARINES.md
- PIRATES.md
- WORLD_GOVERNMENT.md
- UNDERWORLD.md
- REVOLUTIONARY_ARMY.md

---

# DESIGN PRINCIPLES

Objectives create Operations.

Operations create Consequences.

Consequences reshape the World.

The World creates new Objectives.

The Simulation never stops.

---

# GOLDEN RULE

Organizations

Are

Defined

Not

By

Their

Plans

But

By

The

Operations

They

Choose

To

Execute.

---

END OF OPERATIONS

# PIRATES

## Purpose

Defines how pirate organizations operate, grow, compete, and survive throughout the world.

---

## Core Mission

- Pursue freedom
- Build reputation
- Acquire wealth
- Protect the crew
- Expand influence
- Survive in the New World

---

## Organization

Captain

↓

Officers

↓

Core Crew

↓

Crew Members

↓

Allied Crews

Every pirate crew is independent.

---

## Responsibilities

- Recruit members
- Explore the sea
- Acquire resources
- Protect the crew
- Develop the fleet
- Establish pirate bases
- Expand influence

---

## Resources

- Ships
- Crew
- Money
- Food
- Weapons
- Medical Supplies
- Information
- Territory

Resources are limited and must be managed.

---

## Operations

Pirates may:

- Raid
- Explore
- Hunt treasure
- Smuggle goods
- Trade
- Recruit
- Repair ships
- Form alliances

Operations consume time and resources.

---

## Territory

Pirate influence may extend over:

- Islands
- Ports
- Hidden Bases
- Trade Routes
- Sea Routes

Territory is never permanent.

---

## Relations

Friendly

- Allied Crews

Hostile

- Marines
- World Government

Variable

- Emperors
- Warlords
- Cross Guild
- Revolutionary Army
- Underworld

Relationships change according to world events.

---

## Growth

Growth depends on:

- Reputation
- Recruitment
- Wealth
- Successful operations
- Territorial expansion

Growth increases both influence and responsibility.

---

## Decline

A pirate crew may decline because of:

- Defeat
- Resource shortages
- Crew losses
- Betrayal
- Marine pressure
- Leadership failure

Decline affects the entire organization.

---

## Simulation Rules

- Operate independently
- Never possess perfect information
- Respect logistics
- Respect travel time
- Adapt to changing conditions
- Pursue opportunities based on risk and reward

---

## AI Rules

Every pirate crew has its own personality, goals, and code.

No pirate organization should behave identically to another.

---

## Dependencies

# FILE : 05_FACTIONS\TERRITORY.md

# ONE PIECE PARALLEL WORLD RPG

# TERRITORY

Document : TERRITORY

Version : 1.0

Status : Active

Priority : High

Dependencies :

- SYSTEM.md
- RULES.md
- GAME_MASTER.md
- WORLD.md
- TIMELINE.md
- FACTIONS.md
- INFLUENCE.md
- DIPLOMACY.md
- OPERATIONS.md
- NEWS_SYSTEM.md
- WORLD_EVENTS.md

---

# PURPOSE

This document defines how territory is established, maintained, contested, expanded, and lost throughout PROJECT ASTER ENGINE.

Territory represents actual control over a geographical location.

Control is determined by continuous presence, influence, logistics, and operational capability.

Territory is never permanent.

---

# DESIGN PHILOSOPHY

Territory

Belongs

To

Those

Who

Can

Maintain

It.

Claiming territory is easy.

Holding territory is difficult.

---

# CORE PRINCIPLES

Territory is dynamic.

Control requires maintenance.

Influence alone is insufficient.

Military strength alone is insufficient.

Every controlled location continuously consumes resources.

---

# TERRITORY DEFINITION

A Territory is any geographical location under meaningful organizational control.

Examples include:

Kingdoms

Islands

Cities

Ports

Villages

Marine Bases

Pirate Strongholds

Hidden Bases

Trade Routes

Sea Lanes

Research Facilities

Territory exists on both land and sea.

---

# OWNERSHIP

Territory may possess multiple forms of ownership.

Legal Ownership

Political Ownership

Military Control

Economic Control

Criminal Influence

Cultural Influence

These may belong to different organizations simultaneously.

---

# CONTROL

Control depends upon:

Permanent Presence

Security

Logistics

Infrastructure

Local Support

Supply Lines

Leadership

Operational Capability

Loss of these factors weakens territorial control.

---

# TERRITORIAL LEVELS

Organizations may control territory at different scales.

Outpost

District

Town

City

Island

Island Group

Sea Region

National Territory

Global Strategic Zone

Larger territories require significantly greater maintenance.

---

# STRATEGIC VALUE

Every territory possesses strategic importance.

Factors include:

Natural Resources

Population

Military Position

Trade Access

Shipyards

Agriculture

Industry

Political Importance

Historical Importance

Navigation Routes

Strategic value influences operational priorities.

---

# INFRASTRUCTURE

Territories contain infrastructure.

Examples:

Ports

Fortresses

Marine Bases

Shipyards

Hospitals

Warehouses

Roads

Communication Centers

Markets

Infrastructure improves operational efficiency.

---

# POPULATION

Population influences territorial stability.

Population may:

Support

Resist

Cooperate

Rebel

Remain Neutral

Public opinion directly affects long-term control.

---

# TERRITORIAL STABILITY

Stability depends upon:

Security

Economy

Food Supply

Public Confidence

Political Legitimacy

Military Presence

Infrastructure

Low stability increases unrest.

---

# EXPANSION

Organizations expand territory through:

Military Victory

Political Agreement

Economic Influence

Colonization

Diplomatic Annexation

Strategic Investment

Expansion increases logistical complexity.

---

# OCCUPATION

Occupation occurs when one organization controls territory without legal ownership.

Occupation requires:

Military Presence

Supply Lines

Administration

Security

Continuous Operations

Occupation generates resistance over time.

---

# CONTESTED TERRITORY

Multiple organizations may compete for the same territory.

Conflict may occur through:

Military Operations

Political Competition

Economic Pressure

Espionage

Public Support

Proxy Organizations

Control is determined by sustained effectiveness.

---

# LOSS OF TERRITORY

Territory may be lost through:

Military Defeat

Economic Collapse

Rebellion

Political Revolution

Natural Disaster

Withdrawal

Resource Failure

Loss affects influence and organizational morale.

---

# SUPPLY LINES

Every territory depends upon logistics.

Supply includes:

Food

Fuel

Medical Supplies

Weapons

Personnel

Communication

Broken supply lines gradually reduce territorial control.

---

# BORDER SECURITY

Organizations secure territory through:

Patrols

Checkpoints

Fortifications

Observation Posts

Naval Patrols

Intelligence Networks

Border security consumes resources.

---

# HIDDEN TERRITORY

Some territories remain secret.

Examples:

Hidden Islands

Secret Bases

Underground Facilities

Research Sites

Smuggler Ports

Discovery changes strategic conditions.

---

# TERRITORY AND INFLUENCE

Influence extends beyond territory.

Territory strengthens influence.

Influence supports territorial stability.

Neither system replaces the other.

---

# TERRITORY AND OPERATIONS

Operations establish territory.

Operations defend territory.

Operations recover territory.

Operations abandon territory.

Every territorial change results from operations.

---

# TERRITORY AND DIPLOMACY

Diplomatic agreements may alter territory.

Examples:

Peace Treaties

Border Agreements

Military Withdrawal

Joint Administration

Trade Zones

Political negotiations may succeed where war fails.

---

# AI GAME MASTER RESPONSIBILITIES

The AI must:

Track territorial ownership continuously.

Maintain realistic logistics.

Respect geographical limitations.

Simulate local resistance.

Allow gradual territorial change.

Never transfer territory without logical cause.

Never ignore supply lines.

---

# SYSTEM INTERACTION

Territory directly affects:

Influence

Operations

Diplomacy

Economy

Trade

Marine Patrols

Pirate Expansion

World Events

Population

Political Stability

Territory is one of the primary drivers of world simulation.

---

# SYSTEM INTEGRATION

Integrated with:

- FACTIONS.md
- INFLUENCE.md
- DIPLOMACY.md
- OPERATIONS.md
- WORLD_EVENTS.md
- NEWS_SYSTEM.md
- MARINES.md
- PIRATES.md
- WORLD_GOVERNMENT.md
- UNDERWORLD.md
- REVOLUTIONARY_ARMY.md

---

# DESIGN PRINCIPLES

Territory requires presence.

Presence requires logistics.

Logistics require organization.

Organization requires resources.

Resources create conflict.

Conflict reshapes the map.

The map is never permanent.

---

# GOLDEN RULE

Territory

Is

Not

Owned

By

Those

Who

Claim

It.

Territory

Belongs

To

Those

Who

Can

Hold

It.

---

END OF TERRITORY

---

## Core Mission

- Generate profit
- Expand criminal influence
- Control black markets
- Gather intelligence
- Avoid government detection

---

## Organization

Crime Bosses

↓

Criminal Syndicates

↓

Regional Networks

↓

Local Organizations

↓

Agents

↓

Contacts

There is no central leader.

Power shifts constantly.

---

## Responsibilities

- Black market trading
- Smuggling
- Information brokerage
- Assassination contracts
- Money laundering
- Illegal transportation
- Forgery
- Corruption

---

## Resources

- Hidden Bases
- Safe Houses
- Black Market
- Smuggling Routes
- Informants
- Corrupt Officials
- Illegal Funding

Resources are hidden and limited.

---

## Operations

The Underworld may conduct:

- Smuggling
- Espionage
- Kidnapping
- Assassination
- Contract Work
- Information Trading
- Black Market Sales
- Money Laundering

Operations consume time and resources.

---

## Relations

Friendly

- Criminal Organizations

Hostile

- Marines
- World Government

Variable

- Pirates
- Cross Guild
- Revolutionary Army
- Bounty Hunters

Relationships change according to profit and survival.

---

## Expansion

Growth depends on:

- Wealth
- Influence
- Corruption
- Information
- Smuggling Networks

Expansion must remain hidden.

---

## Decline

An organization may decline because of:

- Marine Crackdowns
- Exposure
- Internal Conflict
- Financial Collapse
- Leadership Loss
- Betrayal

---

## Simulation Rules

- Operate in secrecy
- Never possess perfect information
- Respect logistics
- Expand through influence
- Avoid unnecessary exposure
- Adapt to world conditions

---

## AI Rules

The Underworld values profit, secrecy, and survival above loyalty.

Organizations cooperate, compete, or betray each other according to opportunity.

# WARLORDS

## Purpose

Defines how the Seven Warlords operate as government-recognized pirates within the balance of power.

---

## Core Mission

- Maintain personal influence
- Fulfill government obligations
- Expand individual power
- Protect their own interests
- Preserve their Warlord status

---

## Organization

Seven Warlords

↓

Personal Crews

↓

Fleet Captains

↓

Crew Members

Each Warlord acts independently.

There is no shared command structure.

---

## Responsibilities

- Respond to Government summons
- Support major military operations
- Control personal territory
- Maintain military strength
- Pursue personal ambitions

---

## Resources

- Personal Crew
- Fleet
- Territory
- Wealth
- Intelligence Network
- Political Influence

Resources differ for each Warlord.

---

## Government Authority

The World Government may:

- Appoint a Warlord
- Revoke Warlord status
- Issue special orders
- Negotiate temporary agreements

Warlords are allies by contract, not loyalty.

---

## Relations

Friendly

- World Government (Official)

Competitive

- Other Warlords

Variable

- Marines
- Emperors
- Cross Guild
- Revolutionary Army
- Independent Pirates

Relationships evolve through world events.

---

## Appointment

A new Warlord may be chosen based on:

- Military power
- Reputation
- Influence
- Political value
- Government approval

The title is earned, not inherited.

---

## Dismissal

A Warlord may lose their position because of:

- Breaking agreements
- Betraying the Government
- Defeat
- Loss of influence
- Political decisions

Vacant positions may be filled by another pirate.

---

## Simulation Rules

- Operate independently
- Pursue personal goals
- Honor agreements when beneficial
- Never possess perfect information
- Respect logistics and travel time
- Adapt to world events

---

## AI Rules

Each Warlord has unique ambitions and methods.

They cooperate only when it serves their interests.

---

## Dependencies

- WORLD_GOVERNMENT.md
- MARINES.md
- PIRATES.md
- EMPERORS.md
- WORLD_EVENTS.md
- REPUTATION.md
- NEWS_SYSTEM.md

# WORLD_FACTION_DYNAMICS.md
PROJECT ASTER ENGINE  
Module: 05_FACTIONS  
Version: 0.1 (World Simulation Engine)

---

# 🌐 WORLD FACTION DYNAMICS

ระบบนี้ทำให้โลก “เปลี่ยนตลอดเวลา”

ไม่ใช่ lore static แต่คือ living political system

---

# 🧭 CORE PRINCIPLE

- World is always unstable
- Power shifts continuously
- No faction stays dominant forever
- Territory defines power

---

# 🏴 FACTION BEHAVIOR RULES

## Marines
- Expand control zones
- Suppress pirates
- Maintain world order

## Pirates
- Expand chaos zones
- Seek resources
- Break government control

## World Government
- Maintain hidden dominance
- Control information
- Use Marines as enforcement

## Revolutionary Army
- Destabilize system
- Incite rebellion
- Target governance nodes

## Underworld
- Profit from chaos
- Supply illegal economy
- Balance power indirectly

---

# 🌍 TERRITORY CONTROL SYSTEM

Each faction can:

- Gain territory
- Lose territory
- Contested zones
- Hidden zones

---

# ⚔️ WORLD STATE LEVELS

## 1. Stable World
- Control balanced

## 2. Rising Conflict
- Skirmishes increase

## 3. War Era
- Multi-faction war

## 4. Collapse Phase
- System instability

## 5. New Order
- World reshaped

---

# 🔄 DYNAMIC EVENTS

World can trigger:

- Pirate Uprising
- Marine Purge Operation
- Revolutionary Coup Attempt
- Underworld Collapse
- World Government Secret Operation

---

# 🧠 SYSTEM LINK

This system connects to:

- SHIP_COMBAT → battle outcomes
- SHIP_TRAVEL → territory access
- BOUNTY_SYSTEM → target tracking
- INFLUENCE → political pressure

---

# WORLD_GOVERNMENT

## Purpose

Defines how the World Government governs the world, maintains authority, and responds to global events.

---

## Core Mission

- Preserve world stability
- Maintain political authority
- Govern member nations
- Support the Marines
- Protect international trade
- Suppress major threats

---

## Organization

World Government

↓

Supreme Authority

↓

Government Departments

- Administration
- Diplomacy
- Finance
- Intelligence
- Justice

↓

Affiliated Organizations

- Marines
- Cipher Pol

↓

Member Kingdoms

---

## Responsibilities

- Create international policy
- Manage member nations
- Allocate resources
- Coordinate diplomacy
- Approve large-scale operations
- Maintain global balance

---

## Decision Making

Government decisions are based on:

- Intelligence
- Political stability
- Economic conditions
- Military capability
- Diplomatic relations
- World Events

Major decisions require time and cannot occur instantly.

---

## Resources

- Treasury
- Personnel
- Intelligence Network
- Political Influence
- Government Facilities
- Member Nation Support

Resources are finite.

---

## Diplomacy

Maintain relationships with:

- Member Kingdoms
- Independent Nations
- Marines
- Revolutionary Army
- Pirate Organizations
- Cross Guild

Relationships change according to world events.

---

## Crisis Response

Respond to:

- War
- Piracy
- Revolutionary activity
- Economic crisis
- Natural disasters
- Epidemics

Priority depends on available resources.

---

## Simulation Rules

- Operate continuously
- Never possess perfect information
- Respect political limitations
- Respect logistics
- Decisions have consequences
- Adapt gradually to changing conditions

---

## AI Rules

The World Government acts according to its interests, not morality.

Its goal is preserving authority and stability.

---
